<p>The <b>Buffalo Bills</b> are a professional <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> team based in the <a href="/wiki/Buffalo%E2%80%93Niagara_Falls_metropolitan_area" title="Buffalo–Niagara Falls metropolitan area">Buffalo–Niagara Falls metropolitan area</a>. The Bills compete in the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> (NFL), as a member club of the league's <a href="/wiki/American_Football_Conference" title="American Football Conference">American Football Conference</a> (AFC) <a href="/wiki/AFC_East" title="AFC East">East</a> division. The team plays their home games at <a href="/wiki/New_Era_Field" title="New Era Field">New Era Field</a> in <a href="/wiki/Orchard_Park_(town),_New_York" title="Orchard Park (town), New York">Orchard Park, New York</a>. The Bills are the only NFL team that plays its home games in the state of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a> (the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants" title="New York Giants">New York Giants</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a> play at <a href="/wiki/MetLife_Stadium" title="MetLife Stadium">MetLife Stadium</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/East_Rutherford,_New_Jersey" title="East Rutherford, New Jersey">East Rutherford, New Jersey</a>). The Bills conduct summer training camp at <a href="/wiki/St._John_Fisher_College" title="St. John Fisher College">St. John Fisher College</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pittsford_(town),_New_York" title="Pittsford (town), New York">Pittsford, New York</a>, an eastern suburb of <a href="/wiki/Rochester,_New_York" title="Rochester, New York">Rochester, New York</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Bills began play as an original franchise of the <a href="/wiki/American_Football_League" title="American Football League">American Football League</a> (AFL) in <a href="/wiki/1960_American_Football_League_season" title="1960 American Football League season">1960</a>. The club joined the NFL as a result of the <a href="/wiki/AFL%E2%80%93NFL_merger" title="AFL–NFL merger">AFL–NFL merger</a> for the <a href="/wiki/1970_NFL_season" title="1970 NFL season">1970 season</a>. The 1964 and 1965 Bills were the only teams representing Buffalo that won major league professional sports championships ("back-to-back" American Football League Championships). The Bills are the only team to win four consecutive <a href="/wiki/AFC_Championship_Game" title="AFC Championship Game">conference championships</a> and are the only NFL team to lose four consecutive <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a> games. The team was owned by <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Wilson" title="Ralph Wilson">Ralph Wilson</a> from the team's founding in 1960, until his death in 2014 at the age of 95. After his death, Wilson's estate reached an agreement to sell the team to <a href="/wiki/Terrence_Pegula" title="Terrence Pegula">Terry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kim_Pegula" title="Kim Pegula">Kim Pegula</a>, which was approved by the other NFL team owners on October 8, 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The Bills have the <a href="/wiki/List_of_NFL_franchise_post-season_droughts" title="List of NFL franchise post-season droughts">longest active playoff drought</a> in any major professional sport: they have not qualified to play in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Football_League_playoffs" title="National Football League playoffs">NFL playoffs</a> since 1999 and are the only team that has not appeared in the playoffs so far in the 21st century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Buffalo_Bills&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Buffalo_Bills" title="History of the Buffalo Bills">History of the Buffalo Bills</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Buffalo_Bills_seasons" title="List of Buffalo Bills seasons">List of Buffalo Bills seasons</a></div>
<p>The Bills began competitive play in 1960 as a charter member of the <a href="/wiki/American_Football_League" title="American Football League">American Football League</a> led by head coach <a href="/wiki/Buster_Ramsey" title="Buster Ramsey">Buster Ramsey</a> and joined the NFL as part of the <a href="/wiki/AFL%E2%80%93NFL_merger" title="AFL–NFL merger">AFL–NFL merger</a> in 1970.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The Bills won two consecutive American Football League titles in <a href="/wiki/1964_American_Football_League_Championship_Game" title="1964 American Football League Championship Game">1964</a> and <a href="/wiki/1965_American_Football_League_Championship_Game" title="1965 American Football League Championship Game">1965</a>, but the club has yet to win a league championship since.</p>
<p>Once the <a href="/wiki/AFL%E2%80%93NFL_merger" title="AFL–NFL merger">AFL–NFL merger</a> took effect, the Bills became the second NFL team to represent the city; they followed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buffalo_All-Americans" title="Buffalo All-Americans">Buffalo All-Americans</a>, a charter member of the league. Buffalo had been left out of the league since the All-Americans (by that point renamed the Bisons) folded in 1929; the Bills were no less than the third professional non-NFL team to compete in the city before the merger, following the <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Indians" title="Buffalo Indians">Indians/Tigers</a> of the early 1940s and another team named the Bills in the late 1940s. Buffalo's team in the All-America Football Conference (AAFC) in 1946 was the Bisons.</p>
<p>In 1947 a contest was held to rename the team, which was owned by James Breuil of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Frontier_Oil_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Frontier Oil Company (page does not exist)">Frontier Oil Company</a>. The winning entry suggested Bills, reflecting on the famous western frontiersman, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bill_Cody" title="Buffalo Bill Cody">Buffalo Bill Cody</a>. Carrying the "frontier" theme further, the winning contestant offered the team was being supported by Frontier Oil and was "opening a new frontier in sports in Western New York." When Buffalo joined the new American Football League in 1960, the name of the city's earlier pro football entry was adopted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>After being pushed to the brink of failure in the mid-1980s, the collapse of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Football_League" title="United States Football League">United States Football League</a> and a series of high draft picks allowed the Bills to rebuild into a perennial contender in the late 1980s through the mid-1990s, a period in which the team won four consecutive <a href="/wiki/AFC_Championship_Game" title="AFC Championship Game">AFC Championships</a>; the team nevertheless lost all four subsequent <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowls</a>, records in both categories that still stand.</p>
<p>The rise of the division rival <a href="/wiki/New_England_Patriots" title="New England Patriots">New England Patriots</a> under <a href="/wiki/Tom_Brady" title="Tom Brady">Tom Brady</a>, along with numerous failed attempts at rebuilding in the 2000s and 2010s, have prevented the Bills from reaching the playoffs since 1999, a 17-year drought that is the longest active playoff drought in all major professional sports. On October 8, 2014, <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Sabres" title="Buffalo Sabres">Buffalo Sabres</a> owners Terry and Kim Pegula received unanimous approval to acquire the Bills during the NFL owners' meetings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Logos_and_uniforms">Logos and uniforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Buffalo_Bills&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Logos and uniforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AFCE-Uniform-Bills_blue_pants.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="442" data-file-width="1016" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/AFCE-Uniform-Bills_blue_pants.png/250px-AFCE-Uniform-Bills_blue_pants.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/AFCE-Uniform-Bills_blue_pants.png/375px-AFCE-Uniform-Bills_blue_pants.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/AFCE-Uniform-Bills_blue_pants.png/500px-AFCE-Uniform-Bills_blue_pants.png 2x" width="250"/></a>

Bills uniform, 2011</div>

</div>
<p>The Bills' uniforms in its first two seasons were based on those of the <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Lions" title="Detroit Lions">Detroit Lions</a> at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BillsUniformChanges_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-BillsUniformChanges-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gwarnerbuffnews_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-gwarnerbuffnews-10">[10]</a></sup> The team's original colors were Honolulu blue, silver and white, and the helmets were silver with no striping. There was no logo on the helmet, which displayed the players' numbers on each side.</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1962_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="1962 Buffalo Bills season">1962</a>, the standing red bison was designated as the logo and took its place on a white helmet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BillsUniformChanges_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-BillsUniformChanges-9">[9]</a></sup> In 1962, the team's colors also changed to red, white, and blue. The team switched to blue jerseys with red and white "LSU" stripes on the shoulders. the helmets were white with a red center stripe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BillsUniformChanges_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-BillsUniformChanges-9">[9]</a></sup> The jerseys again saw a change in <a href="/wiki/1964_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="1964 Buffalo Bills season">1964</a> when the shoulder stripes were replaced by a distinctive stripe pattern on the sleeves consisting of four stripes, two thicker inner stripes and two thinner outer stripes all bordered by red piping. By <a href="/wiki/1965_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="1965 Buffalo Bills season">1965</a>, red and blue center stripes were put on the helmets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Bills introduced blue pants worn with the white jerseys in <a href="/wiki/1973_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="1973 Buffalo Bills season">1973</a>, the last year of the standing buffalo helmet. The blue pants remained through <a href="/wiki/1985_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="1985 Buffalo Bills season">1985</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The face mask on the helmet was blue from <a href="/wiki/1974_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="1974 Buffalo Bills season">1974</a> through <a href="/wiki/1986_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="1986 Buffalo Bills season">1986</a> before changing to white.</p>
<p>The standing bison logo was replaced by a blue charging one with a red slanting stripe streaming from its horn. The newer emblem, which is still the primary one used by the franchise, was designed by aerospace designer Stevens Wright in 1974.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1984_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="1984 Buffalo Bills season">1984</a>, the helmet's background color was changed from white to red, primarily to help Bills quarterback <a href="/wiki/Joe_Ferguson" title="Joe Ferguson">Joe Ferguson</a> distinguish them more readily from three of their division rivals at that time, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Colts" title="Baltimore Colts">Baltimore Colts</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Dolphins" title="Miami Dolphins">Miami Dolphins</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Patriots" title="New England Patriots">New England Patriots</a>, who all also wore white helmets at that point. Ferguson said "Everyone we played had white helmets at that time. Our new head coach Kay Stephenson just wanted to get more of a contrast on the field that may help spot a receiver down the field."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> (The Patriots now use a silver helmet, the Colts have since been realigned to the <a href="/wiki/AFC_South" title="AFC South">AFC South</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a>, who switched to green helmets after the <a href="/wiki/1977_New_York_Jets_season" title="1977 New York Jets season">1977 season</a>, have since switched back to white helmets.)</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/2002_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="2002 Buffalo Bills season">2002</a>, under the direction of general manager <a href="/wiki/Tom_Donahoe" title="Tom Donahoe">Tom Donahoe</a>, the Bills' uniforms went through radical changes. A darker shade of blue was introduced as the main jersey color, and nickel gray was introduced as an accent color. Both the blue and white jerseys featured red side panels. The white jerseys included a dark blue shoulder yoke and royal blue numbers. The helmet remained primarily red with one navy blue, two nickel, two royal blue, two white stripes, and white face mask. A new logo, a stylized "B" consisting of two bullets and a more detailed buffalo head on top, was proposed and had been released (it can be seen on a few baseball caps that were released for sale), but fan backlash led to the team retaining the running bison logo. The helmet logo adopted in 1974—a charging royal blue bison, with a red streak, white horn and eyeball—remained unchanged.</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/2005_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="2005 Buffalo Bills season">2005</a>, the Bills revived the standing bison helmet and uniform of the mid-1960s as a throwback uniform.</p>
<p>The Bills usually wore the all-blue combination at home and the all-white combination on the road when not wearing the throwback uniforms. They stopped wearing blue-on-white after <a href="/wiki/2006_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="2006 Buffalo Bills season">2006</a>, while the white-on-blue was not worn after <a href="/wiki/2007_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="2007 Buffalo Bills season">2007</a>.</p>
<p>For the <a href="/wiki/2011_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="2011 Buffalo Bills season">2011 season</a>, the Bills unveiled a new uniform design, an updated rendition of the 1975–83 design. This change includes a return to the white helmets with "charging buffalo" logo, and a return to <a href="/wiki/Royal_blue" title="Royal blue">royal blue</a> instead of <a href="/wiki/Navy_blue" title="Navy blue">navy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Buffalo sporadically wore white at home in the 1980s, but stopped doing so before their Super Bowl years. On November 6, 2011, against the New York Jets, the Bills wore white at home for the first time since <a href="/wiki/1986_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="1986 Buffalo Bills season">1986</a>. Since 2011, the Bills have worn white for a home game either with their primary uniform or a throwback set.</p>
<p>The Bills' uniform received minor alterations as part of the league's new uniform contract with <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a>. The new Nike uniform was unveiled on April 3, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>On November 12, 2015, the Bills and the New York Jets became the first two teams to participate in the NFL's Color Rush uniform initiative, with Buffalo wearing an all-red combination for the first time in team history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Playoffs">Playoffs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Buffalo_Bills&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Playoffs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1963_AFL_season" title="1963 AFL season">1963 AFL Eastern Division Playoff</a>: <a href="/wiki/1963_Boston_Patriots_season" title="1963 Boston Patriots season">Boston Patriots</a> 26, <a href="/wiki/1963_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="1963 Buffalo Bills season">Buffalo Bills</a> 8</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1964_AFL_season" title="1964 AFL season">1964 AFL Championship</a>: <a href="/wiki/1964_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="1964 Buffalo Bills season">Buffalo Bills</a> 20, <a href="/wiki/1964_San_Diego_Chargers_season" title="1964 San Diego Chargers season">San Diego Chargers</a> 7</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1965_AFL_season" title="1965 AFL season">1965 AFL Championship</a>: <a href="/wiki/1965_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="1965 Buffalo Bills season">Buffalo Bills</a> 23, <a href="/wiki/1965_San_Diego_Chargers_season" title="1965 San Diego Chargers season">San Diego Chargers</a> 0</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1966_AFL_season" title="1966 AFL season">1966 AFL Championship</a>: <a href="/wiki/1966_Kansas_City_Chiefs_season" title="1966 Kansas City Chiefs season">Kansas City Chiefs</a> 31, <a href="/wiki/1966_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="1966 Buffalo Bills season">Buffalo Bills</a> 7</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Players">Players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Buffalo_Bills&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retired_numbers">Retired numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Buffalo_Bills&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Retired numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center">
<tr>
<td colspan="5" style="background: #00338D; color:white;;"><b>Buffalo Bills retired numbers</b></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th style="background: #C60C30; color:#FFFFFF;;" width="40px">No.</th>
<th style="background: #C60C30; color:#FFFFFF;;" width="100px">Player</th>
<th style="background: #C60C30; color:#FFFFFF;;" width="40px">Position</th>
<th style="background: #C60C30; color:#FFFFFF;;" width="100px">Tenure</th>
<th style="background: #C60C30; color:#FFFFFF;;" width="300px">Notes</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>12</b></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Jim_Kelly" title="Jim Kelly">Jim Kelly</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Quarterback" title="Quarterback">QB</a></td>
<td>1986–96<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reduced_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-reduced-21">[21]</a></sup></td>
<td style="text-align:left;">Previously worn by <a href="/wiki/Joe_Ferguson" title="Joe Ferguson">Joe Ferguson</a>, QB, 1973–84; and <a href="/wiki/Daryle_Lamonica" title="Daryle Lamonica">Daryle Lamonica</a>, QB, 1963–66</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>78</b></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Bruce_Smith_(defensive_end)" title="Bruce Smith (defensive end)">Bruce Smith</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Defensive_end" title="Defensive end">DE</a></td>
<td>1985–99<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SmithHumbledAppreciative_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-SmithHumbledAppreciative-22">[22]</a></sup></td>
<td style="text-align:left;">Previously worn by <a href="/wiki/Tom_Day" title="Tom Day">Tom Day</a>, DE, 1961–68; <a href="/wiki/Dave_Foley_(American_football)" title="Dave Foley (American football)">Dave Foley</a>, OT, 1972–77; <a href="/wiki/Gene_Grabosky" title="Gene Grabosky">Gene Grabosky</a>, OT, 1960; and <a href="/wiki/Scott_Hutchinson_(American_football)" title="Scott Hutchinson (American football)">Scott Hutchinson</a>, DE, 1978–80, 1983</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The Buffalo Bills have retired two numbers in franchise history: No. 12 for <a href="/wiki/Jim_Kelly" title="Jim Kelly">Jim Kelly</a> and No. 78 for <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Smith_(defensive_end)" title="Bruce Smith (defensive end)">Bruce Smith</a>. Despite the fact that the Bills have only retired two jersey numbers in franchise history, the team has other numbers no longer issued to any player or in reduced circulation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reduced_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-reduced-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SmithHumbledAppreciative_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-SmithHumbledAppreciative-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt><b>Unofficially retired:</b></dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>32 <a href="/wiki/O._J._Simpson" title="O. J. Simpson">O. J. Simpson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Running_back" title="Running back">RB</a>, 1969–77</li>
<li>34 <a href="/wiki/Thurman_Thomas" title="Thurman Thomas">Thurman Thomas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Running_back" title="Running back">RB</a>, 1988–99; previously worn by <a href="/wiki/Cookie_Gilchrist" title="Cookie Gilchrist">Cookie Gilchrist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Running_back" title="Running back">RB</a>, 1962–64</li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt><b>Reduced circulation:</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reduced_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-reduced-21">[21]</a></sup></dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>44 <a href="/wiki/Elbert_Dubenion" title="Elbert Dubenion">Elbert Dubenion</a>, WR, 1960–68</li>
<li>66 <a href="/wiki/Billy_Shaw" title="Billy Shaw">Billy Shaw</a>, OG, 1961–69</li>
<li>83 <a href="/wiki/Andre_Reed" title="Andre Reed">Andre Reed</a>, WR, 1985–99 <i>(<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lee_Evans_III" title="Lee Evans III">Lee Evans III</a> wore #83 by special permission)</i></li>
</ul>
<p>Since the earliest days of the team, the number 31 was not supposed to be issued to any other player. The Bills had stationery and various other team merchandise showing a running player wearing that number, and it was not supposed to represent any specific person, but the 'spirit of the team.' In the first three decades of the team's existence, the number 31 was only seen once: in 1969, when reserve running back <a href="/wiki/Preston_Ridlehuber" title="Preston Ridlehuber">Preston Ridlehuber</a> damaged his number 36 jersey during a game, equipment manager Tony Marchitte gave him the number 31 jersey to wear while repairing the number 36. The number 31 was not issued again until 1990 when first round draft choice <a href="/wiki/James_Williams_(defensive_back)" title="James Williams (defensive back)">James (J.D.) Williams</a> wore it for his first two seasons.</p>
<p>Number 15 was historically only issued sparingly after the retirement of <a href="/wiki/Jack_Kemp" title="Jack Kemp">Jack Kemp</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reduced_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-reduced-21">[21]</a></sup> but is apparently now in general circulation; <a href="/wiki/Brandon_Tate" title="Brandon Tate">Brandon Tate</a> currently wears the number.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_and_television">Radio and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Buffalo_Bills&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Radio and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Buffalo_Bills_broadcasters" title="List of Buffalo Bills broadcasters">List of Buffalo Bills broadcasters</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bills_Radio_Network" title="Buffalo Bills Radio Network">Buffalo Bills Radio Network</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bills_Radio_Network" title="Buffalo Bills Radio Network">Buffalo Bills Radio Network</a> is flagshipped at <a href="/wiki/WGR" title="WGR">WGR</a>, AM 550 in Buffalo. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Murphy_(announcer)" title="John Murphy (announcer)">John Murphy</a> is the team's current <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sports_commentary" title="Sports commentary">play-by-play</a> announcer; he was a <a href="/wiki/Color_commentator" title="Color commentator">color commentator</a> alongside, and eventually succeeded, longtime voice <a href="/wiki/Van_Miller" title="Van Miller">Van Miller</a> after Miller's retirement at the end of the <a href="/wiki/2003_NFL_season" title="2003 NFL season">2003 NFL season</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mark_Kelso" title="Mark Kelso">Mark Kelso</a> serves as the color analyst. The Bills radio network has approximately seventeen affiliates in <a href="/wiki/Upstate_New_York" title="Upstate New York">upstate New York</a> and one affiliate, <a href="/wiki/CJCL" title="CJCL">CJCL</a> 590AM (The Fan) in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>. As of early 2012, it is composed mostly of <a href="/wiki/WGR" title="WGR">WGR</a>, Entercom's sister stations <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WCMF" title="WCMF">WCMF</a> (96.5 FM) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WROC-AM" title="WROC-AM">WROC-AM</a> 950 in Rochester, and a fleet of independent AM and FM stations across upstate New York from Jamestown east to Albany. Previous flagship <a href="/wiki/Citadel_Broadcasting" title="Citadel Broadcasting">Citadel Broadcasting</a> was purchased by <a href="/wiki/Cumulus_Media" title="Cumulus Media">Cumulus Media</a>, who in turn ceased carrying Bills games at the end of the 2011 season, leaving the network without affiliates in Syracuse, Binghamton, and Erie. (The Syracuse affiliations were later picked up by <a href="/wiki/Galaxy_Communications" title="Galaxy Communications">Galaxy Communications</a>.) Buffalo is one of ten teams contracted with <a href="/wiki/Compass_Media_Networks" title="Compass Media Networks">Compass Media Networks</a> to syndicate selected games nationwide.</p>
<p>During the preseason, most games are televised on Buffalo's <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> affiliate, <a href="/wiki/WKBW-TV" title="WKBW-TV">WKBW-TV</a> channel 7, with several other affiliates in <a href="/wiki/Western_New_York" title="Western New York">western New York</a>. These games are simulcast on sister stations <a href="/wiki/WTVH" title="WTVH">WTVH</a> in Syracuse, <a href="/wiki/WICU-TV" title="WICU-TV">WICU</a> in Erie, <a href="/wiki/WHAM-TV" title="WHAM-TV">WHAM-TV</a> in Rochester, and for a period, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CITY-TV" title="CITY-TV">CITY-TV</a> in Toronto. CBS analyst and former Bills special teams player <a href="/wiki/Steve_Tasker" title="Steve Tasker">Steve Tasker</a> does color commentary on these games; the play-by-play position is rotated between his CBS partner <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andrew_Catalon" title="Andrew Catalon">Andrew Catalon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rob_Stone" title="Rob Stone">Rob Stone</a>. WHAM-TV sports anchor <a href="/wiki/Mike_Catalana" title="Mike Catalana">Mike Catalana</a> is the sideline reporter. Since 2008, preseason games have been broadcast in <a href="/wiki/High-definition_television" title="High-definition television">high definition</a>.</p>
<p>Beginning in the 2016 season, as per a new rights deal which covers rights to the team as well as its sister <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">NHL</a> franchise, the <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Sabres" title="Buffalo Sabres">Buffalo Sabres</a>, most team-related programming, including studio programming and the coach's show, was re-located to <a href="/wiki/MSG_Western_New_York" title="MSG Western New York">MSG Western New York</a>—a joint venture of MSG and the team ownership. Preseason games will continue to air in simulcast on WKBW.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn-msgwny_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-bn-msgwny-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the event regular season games are broadcast by <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>, WKBW-TV will also hold the broadcast rights to that contest, with the station having won back the rights to cable games after <a href="/wiki/WBBZ-TV" title="WBBZ-TV">WBBZ-TV</a> held the rights for 2012 and 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Training_camp_sites">Training camp sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Buffalo_Bills&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Training camp sites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>1960–1962 <a href="/wiki/Roycroft" title="Roycroft">Roycroft Inn</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Aurora,_New_York" title="East Aurora, New York">East Aurora, New York</a></li>
<li>1963–1967 Camelot Hotel, <a href="/wiki/Blasdell,_New_York" title="Blasdell, New York">Blasdell, New York</a></li>
<li>1968–1980 <a href="/wiki/Niagara_University" title="Niagara University">Niagara University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lewiston,_New_York" title="Lewiston, New York">Lewiston, New York</a></li>
<li>1981–1999 <a href="/wiki/State_University_of_New_York_at_Fredonia" title="State University of New York at Fredonia">State University of New York at Fredonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fredonia,_New_York" title="Fredonia, New York">Fredonia, New York</a></li>
<li>2000–present, <a href="/wiki/St._John_Fisher_College" title="St. John Fisher College">St. John Fisher College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pittsford_(village),_New_York" title="Pittsford (village), New York">Pittsford, New York</a></li>
</ul>
<p><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascots.2C_cheerleaders_and_marching_band">Mascots, cheerleaders and marching band</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Buffalo_Bills&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Mascots, cheerleaders and marching band">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Bills' official mascot is <a href="/wiki/Billy_Buffalo" title="Billy Buffalo">Billy Buffalo</a>, an eight-foot tall, anthropomorphic blue <a href="/wiki/American_bison" title="American bison">American bison</a> who wears the jersey "number" BB.</p>
<p>The Bills currently do not have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Football_League_cheerleading" title="National Football League cheerleading">cheerleaders</a>. The Bills employed the <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Jills" title="Buffalo Jills">Buffalo Jills</a>, an independent organization, from 1967 to 2013; the Jills suspended operations prior to the 2014 season due to legal actions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Bills are one of six teams in the NFL to designate an official marching band or drumline (the others being the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Ravens" title="Baltimore Ravens">Baltimore Ravens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_Redskins" title="Washington Redskins">Washington Redskins</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Panthers" title="Carolina Panthers">Carolina Panthers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Seahawks" title="Seattle Seahawks">Seattle Seahawks</a>). Since the last game of the 2013 season, this position has been served by the Stampede Drumline, known outside of Buffalo as Downbeat Percussion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The Bills have also used the full marching bands from Attica High School, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">University of Pittsburgh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_University" title="Syracuse University">Syracuse University</a> at home games in recent years.</p>
<p>The Bills have several theme songs associated with them. One is a variation of the Isley Brothers hit "<a href="/wiki/Shout_(The_Isley_Brothers_song)" title="Shout (The Isley Brothers song)">Shout</a>", recorded by Scott Kemper,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> which served as the Bills' official promotional song from 1987 through 1990s. It was officially replaced circa 2000 with "The Power of the Bills", although "Shout" remains in use. The Bills' unofficial <a href="/wiki/Fight_song" title="Fight song">fight song</a>, "Go Bills", was penned by Bills head coach <a href="/wiki/Marv_Levy" title="Marv Levy">Marv Levy</a> in the mid-1990s on a <a href="/wiki/Friendly_political_wager" title="Friendly political wager">friendly wager</a> with his players that he will write the song if the team won a particular game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Supporters">Supporters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Buffalo_Bills&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Supporters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <b>Bills Backers</b> are the official fan organization of the Buffalo Bills. It has over 200 chapters across North America, Europe and Oceania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Also notable is the <i>Bills Mafia</i>, a collection of Bills fans organized via <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> beginning in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Bills are one of the favorite teams of <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> announcer <a href="/wiki/Chris_Berman" title="Chris Berman">Chris Berman</a>, who picked the Bills to reach the Super Bowl nearly every year in the 1990s. Berman often uses the catchphrase "No one <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Circle_the_wagons" title="Circle the wagons">circles the wagons</a> like the Buffalo Bills!" Berman gave the induction speech for Bills owner <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Wilson" title="Ralph Wilson">Ralph Wilson</a> when Wilson was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Pro_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="Pro Football Hall of Fame">Pro Football Hall of Fame</a> in 2009.</p>
<p>The Bills were also the favorite team of late <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> political commentator <a href="/wiki/Tim_Russert" title="Tim Russert">Tim Russert</a>, a <a href="/wiki/South_Buffalo,_Buffalo,_New_York" title="South Buffalo, Buffalo, New York">South Buffalo</a> native, who often referred to the Bills on his Sunday morning talk show, <i><a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Press" title="Meet the Press">Meet the Press</a></i>. (His son, <a href="/wiki/Luke_Russert" title="Luke Russert">Luke</a>, is also a notable fan of the team.) <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Wolf_Blitzer" title="Wolf Blitzer">Wolf Blitzer</a>, also a Buffalo native, has proclaimed he is also a fan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>ESPN anchor <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Connors" title="Kevin Connors">Kevin Connors</a> is also a noted Bills fan, dating to his time attending <a href="/wiki/Ithaca_College" title="Ithaca College">Ithaca College</a>. Actor <a href="/wiki/Nick_Bakay" title="Nick Bakay">Nick Bakay</a>, a Buffalo native, is also a well-known Bills fan; he has discussed the team in segments of <a href="/wiki/NFL_Top_10" title="NFL Top 10">NFL Top 10</a>. Character actor <a href="/wiki/William_Fichtner" title="William Fichtner">William Fichtner</a>, raised in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cheektowaga,_New_York" title="Cheektowaga, New York">Cheektowaga</a>, is a fan, and did a commercial for the team in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> In 2015, Fichtner also narrated the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESPN_30_for_30" title="ESPN 30 for 30">ESPN 30 for 30</a> documentary on the Bills four Super Bowl appearances, "<a href="/wiki/Four_Falls_of_Buffalo" title="Four Falls of Buffalo">Four Falls of Buffalo</a>".</p>
<p>Bills fans are particularly well known for their wearing of <a href="/wiki/Zubaz" title="Zubaz">Zubaz</a> zebra-printed sportswear; so much is the association between Bills fans and Zubaz that when a revival of the company opened their first brick-and-mortar storefront, it chose Western New York as its first location.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Buffalo_Bills&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Buffalo's <a href="/wiki/Bills%E2%80%93Dolphins_rivalry" title="Bills–Dolphins rivalry">rivalry</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Dolphins" title="Miami Dolphins">Miami Dolphins</a> is referenced on <a href="/wiki/Steve_Martin" title="Steve Martin">Steve Martin</a>'s 1979 album <i><a href="/wiki/Comedy_Is_Not_Pretty!" title="Comedy Is Not Pretty!">Comedy Is Not Pretty!</a></i> on the track "How To Meet A Girl." On the track, Martin simulates chatter about football at a party and one "partier" expresses disbelief Buffalo could beat Miami – at the time of the album's release, the Dolphins had won 18 straight games over the Bills.</p>
<p>In the 1996 <i><a href="/wiki/The_X-Files" title="The X-Files">X-Files</a></i> episode "<a href="/wiki/Musings_of_a_Cigarette_Smoking_Man" title="Musings of a Cigarette Smoking Man">Musings of a Cigarette Smoking Man</a>", the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Smoking_Man" title="The Smoking Man">titular character</a>, a member of <a href="/wiki/Syndicate_(The_X-Files)" title="Syndicate (The X-Files)">a shadowy government cabal</a>, states the Buffalo Bills will not win a Super Bowl while he lives.</p>
<p>The Buffalo Bills were featured on the direct-to-TV movie <i><a href="/wiki/Second_String" title="Second String">Second String</a></i>, and in the <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Gallo" title="Vincent Gallo">Vincent Gallo</a> drama <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buffalo_66" title="Buffalo 66">Buffalo 66</a></i>.</p>
<p>Actor <a href="/wiki/Dean_Cain" title="Dean Cain">Dean Cain</a> was briefly a member of the Bills. Because of this, references to the Bills have appeared in the television series <i><a href="/wiki/Lois_%26_Clark:_The_New_Adventures_of_Superman" title="Lois &amp; Clark: The New Adventures of Superman">Lois &amp; Clark: The New Adventures of Superman</a></i>, in which Cain played <a href="/wiki/Superman" title="Superman">the title character</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Lois_%26_Clark:_The_New_Adventures_of_Superman_(season_4)" title="Lois &amp; Clark: The New Adventures of Superman (season 4)">first episode of season four</a>, titled "Lord of the Flys", Clark picks up a blue Buffalo Bills hat with the Charging Buffalo emblem in the center and uses it to help disguise himself. In a later episode, he lets it be known the Metropolis Mammoths were playing the Bills.</p>
<p>In an April 2011 episode of the television series <i><a href="/wiki/30_Rock" title="30 Rock">30 Rock</a></i>, titled "<a href="/wiki/100_(30_Rock)" title="100 (30 Rock)">100</a>", <a href="/wiki/Alec_Baldwin" title="Alec Baldwin">Alec Baldwin</a>'s character <a href="/wiki/Jack_Donaghy" title="Jack Donaghy">Jack Donaghy</a> discovers that, in an alternate future, he would not only be wealthier and more successful, but he would also be the owner of a "New York football team." He later is disappointed to learn the team is not the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants" title="New York Giants">New York Giants</a> or <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a>, but the Buffalo Bills.</p>
<p>The Bills are the team that eventually unseats the Orlando Breakers, the fictional NFL team that serves as the focus of the sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/Coach_(TV_series)" title="Coach (TV series)">Coach</a></i> in later seasons, in the playoffs.</p>
<p>In a March 2014 episode of the television series <i><a href="/wiki/Family_Guy" title="Family Guy">Family Guy</a></i> entitled "<a href="/wiki/3_Acts_of_God" title="3 Acts of God">3 Acts of God</a>", <a href="/wiki/Peter_Griffin" title="Peter Griffin">Peter Griffin</a>—along with his family and friends—attends a game between the Buffalo Bills and New England Patriots at <a href="/wiki/Gillette_Stadium" title="Gillette Stadium">Gillette Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Foxborough,_Massachusetts" title="Foxborough, Massachusetts">Foxborough, Massachusetts</a>, which the Bills win. The episode also features Bills players <a href="/wiki/Mario_Williams" title="Mario Williams">Mario Williams</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C.J._Spiller" title="C.J. Spiller">C.J. Spiller</a> guest starring as themselves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several former Buffalo Bills players have earned a name in politics after their playing careers had ended, almost always as members of the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a>. The most famous of these was quarterback <a href="/wiki/Jack_Kemp" title="Jack Kemp">Jack Kemp</a>, who was elected to <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">the U.S. House of Representatives</a> from <a href="/wiki/Western_New_York" title="Western New York">Western New York</a> in 1971—two years after his playing career ended and remained there for nearly two decades, serving as the Republican Party nominee for <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">Vice President of the United States</a> under <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dole" title="Bob Dole">Bob Dole</a> in <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1996" title="United States presidential election, 1996">1996</a>. Kemp's backup, <a href="/wiki/Ed_Rutkowski" title="Ed Rutkowski">Ed Rutkowski</a>, served as county executive of <a href="/wiki/Erie_County,_New_York" title="Erie County, New York">Erie County</a> from 1979 to 1987. Former tight end <a href="/wiki/Jay_Riemersma" title="Jay Riemersma">Jay Riemersma</a>, defensive tackle <a href="/wiki/Fred_Smerlas" title="Fred Smerlas">Fred Smerlas</a> and defensive end <a href="/wiki/Phil_Hansen_(American_football)" title="Phil Hansen (American football)">Phil Hansen</a> have all run for Congress, though all three either lost or withdrew from their respective races. Quarterback <a href="/wiki/Jim_Kelly" title="Jim Kelly">Jim Kelly</a> and running back <a href="/wiki/Thurman_Thomas" title="Thurman Thomas">Thurman Thomas</a> have also both been mentioned as potential candidates for political office, although both have declined all requests to date.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Buffalo_Bills&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
